 CHAPTER XXXV . 

 the HUSH that succeed the TEMPEST . 

 Robert Audley follow his uncle into the vestibule after Sir Michael have speak those few quiet word which sound the death - knell of his hope and love . Heaven know how much the young man have fear the coming of this day . it have come ; and though there have be no great outburst of despair , no whirlwind of stormy grief , no loud tempest of anguish and tear , Robert take no comforting thought from the unnatural stillness . he know enough to know that Sir Michael Audley go away with the barbed arrow , which his nephew 's hand have send home to its aim , rankle in his tortured heart ; he know that this strange and icy calm be the first numbness of a heart stricken by grief so unexpected as for a time to be render almost incomprehensible by a blank stupor of astonishment ; he know that when this dull quiet have pass away , when little by little , and one by one , each horrible feature of the sufferer 's sorrow become first dimly apparent and then terribly familiar to he , the storm would burst in fatal fury , and tempest of tear and cruel thunder - clap of agony would rend that generous heart . 

 Robert have hear of case in which man of his uncle 's age have bear some great grief , as Sir Michael have bear this , with a strange quiet ; and have go away from those who would have comfort they , and whose anxiety have be relieve by this patient stillness , to fall down upon the ground and die under the blow which at first have only stun he . he remember case in which paralysis and apoplexy have stricken man as strong as his uncle in the first hour of the horrible affliction ; and he linger in the lamp - light vestibule , wonder whether it be not his duty to be with Sir Michael to be near he , in case of any emergency , and to accompany he wherever he go .

I have do what I believe to have be my solemn duty , yet I should scarcely wonder if I have render myself forever hateful to he . it be well he should fight the battle alone .  CHAPTER XXXVI . 

 DR . MOSGRAVE 's advice . 

 my lady sleep . through that long winter night she sleep soundly . criminal have often so sleep their last sleep upon earth ; and have be find in the gray morning slumber peacefully , by the jailer who come to wake they .

 the physician from Saville Row be a tall man of about fifty year of age . he be thin and sallow , with lantern jaw , and eye of a pale , feeble gray , that seem as if they have once be blue , and have fade by the progress of time to their present neutral shade . however powerful the science of medicine as wield by Dr. Alwyn Mosgrave , it have not be strong enough to put flesh upon his bone , or brightness into his face . he have a strangely expressionless , and yet strangely attentive countenance . he have the face of a man who have spend the great part of his life in listen to other people , and who have part with his own individuality and his own passion at the very outset of his career .

"

I will tell you what she be , Mr. Audley . she be dangerous ! "

"

 CHAPTER XXXVIII .

 Robert have only the third letter to open the letter which he have place in his bosom while he read the other ; he tear open the envelope , handle it carefully and tenderly as he have do before . 

 the letter be as brief as Sir Michael 's . it contain only these few line : 

 " DEAR MR . AUDLEY the rector of this place have be twice to see Marks , the man you save in the fire at the Castle Inn . he lie in a very precarious state at his mother 's cottage , near Audley Court , and be not expect to live many day . his wife be attend he , and both he and she have express a most earnest desire that you should see he before he die . pray come without delay . 

 " yours very sincerely , 

 " CLARA TALBOYS . 

 " Mount Stanning Rectory , March 6 . " 

 Robert Audley fold this letter very reverently , and place it underneath that part of his waistcoat which might be suppose to cover the region of his heart . have do this , he seat himself in his favorite arm - chair , fill and light a pipe and smoke it out , star reflectingly at the fire as long as his tobacco last . " what can that man mark want with I , " think the barrister . " he be afraid to die until he have make confession , perhaps . he wish to tell I that which I know already the story of my lady 's crime . I know that he be in the secret . I be sure of it even upon the night on which I first see he . he know the secret , and he trade on it . " 

 Robert Audley shrink strangely from return to Essex . how should he meet Clara Talboys now that he know the secret of her brother 's fate ? how many lie he should have to tell , or how much equivocation he must use in order to keep the truth from she ? yet would there be any mercy in tell that horrible story , the knowledge of which must cast a blight upon her youth , and blot out every hope she have even secretly cherish ? he know by his own experience how possible it be to hope against hope , and to hope unconsciously ; and he could not bear that her heart should be crush as his have be by the knowledge of the truth . " well that she should hope vainly to the last , " he think ; " well that she should go through life seek the clew to her lose brother 's fate , than that I should give that clew into her hand , and say , ' our bad fear be realize . the brother you love have be foully murder in the early promise of his youth . ' " 

 but Clara Talboys have write to he , implore he to return to Essex without delay . could he refuse to do her bidding , however painful its accomplishment might be ? and again , the man be die , perhaps , and have implore to see he . would it not be cruel to refuse to go to delay an hour unnecessarily ? he look at his watch . it want only five minute to nine . there be no train to Audley after the Ipswich mail , which leave London at half - past eight ; but there be a train that leave Shoreditch at eleven , and stop at Brentwood between twelve and one . Robert decide upon go by this train , and walk the distance between Brentwood and Audley , which be upwards of six mile . 

 Fleet street be quiet and lonely at this late hour , and Robert Audley be in a ghost - see mood , would have be scarcely astonished have he see Johnson 's set come roystere westward in the lamp - light , or blind John Milton grope his way down the step before Saint Bride 's Church . 

 Mr. Audley hail a hansom at the corner of Farrington street , and be rattle rapidly away across tenantless Smithfield market , and into a labyrinth of dingy street that bring he out upon the broad grandeur of Finsbury Pavement . 

 the hansom rattle up the steep and stony approach to Shoreditch Station , and deposit Robert at the door of that unlovely temple . there be very few people go to travel by this midnight train , and Robert walk up and down the long wooden platform , read the huge advertisement whose gaunt lettering look wan and ghastly in the dim lamplight . 

 he have the carriage in which he sit all to himself . all to himself do I say ? have he not lately summon to his side that ghostly company which of all companionship be the most tenacious ? the shadow of George Talboys pursue he , even in the comfortable first - class carriage , and be behind he when he look out of the window , and be yet far ahead of he and the rush engine , in that thicket toward which the train be speed , by the side of the unhallowed hiding - place in which the mortal remain of the dead man lie , neglect and uncare for . 

 " I must give my lose friend decent burial , " Robert think , as the chill wind sweep across the flat landscape , and strike he with such frozen breath as might have emanate from the lip of the dead . " I must do it ; or I shall die of some panic like this which have seize upon I to - night . I must do it ; at any peril ; at any cost . even at the price of that revelation which will bring the mad woman back from her safe hiding - place , and place she in a criminal dock . " he be glad when the train stop at Brentwood at a few minute after twelve . 

 it be half - past one o'clock when the night wanderer enter the village of Audley , and it be only there that he remember that Clara Talboys have omit to give he any direction by which he might find the cottage in which Luke Marks lay . 

 " it be Dawson who recommend that the poor creature should be take to his mother 's cottage , " Robert think , by - and - by , " and , I dare say . Dawson have attend he ever since the fire . he will be able to tell I the way to the cottage . " 

 act upon this idea , Mr. Audley stop at the house in which Helen Talboys have live before her second marriage . the door of the little surgery be ajar , and there be a light burn within . Robert push the door open and peep in . the surgeon be stand at the mahogany counter , mix a draught in a glass measure , with his hat close beside he . late as it be , he have evidently only just come in . the harmonious snoring of his assistant sound from a little room within the surgery . 

 " I be sorry to disturb you , Mr. Dawson , " Robert say , apologetically , as the surgeon look up and recognize he , " but I have come down to see Marks , who , I hear , be in a very bad way , and I want you to tell I the way to his mother 's cottage . " 

 " I will show you the way , Mr. Audley , " answer the surgeon , " I be go there this minute . " 

 " the man be very bad , then ? " 

 " so bad that he can be no bad . the change that can happen be that change which will take he beyond the reach of any earthly suffering . " 

 " strange ! " exclaim Robert . " he do not appear to be much burn . " 

 " he be not much burn . have he be , I should never have recommend his being remove from Mount Stanning . it be the shock that have do the business . he have be in a rag fever for the last two day ; but to - night he be much calm , and I be afraid , before to - morrow night , we shall have see the last of he . " 

 " he have ask to see I , I be tell , " say Mr. Audley . 

 " yes , " answer the surgeon , carelessly . " a sick man 's fancy , no doubt . you drag he out of the house , and do your good to save his life . I dare say , rough and boorish as the poor fellow be , he think a good deal of that . " 

 they have leave the surgery , the door of which Mr. Dawson have lock behind he . there be money in the till , perhaps , for surely the village apothecary could not have fear that the most daring housebreaker would imperil his liberty in the pursuit of blue pill and colocynth , of salt and senna . 

 the surgeon lead the way along the silent street , and presently turn into a lane at the end of which Robert Audley see the wan glimmer of a light ; a light which tell of the watch that be keep by the sick and die ; a pale , melancholy light , which always have a dismal aspect when look upon in this silent hour betwixt night and morning . it shine from the window of the cottage in which Luke Marks lay , watch by his wife and mother . 

 Mr. Dawson lift the latch , and walk into the common room of the little tenement , follow by Robert Audley . it be empty , but a feeble tallow candle , with a broken back , and a long , cauliflower - head wick , sputter upon the table . the sick man lie in the room above . 

 " shall I tell he you be here ? " ask Mr. Dawson . 

 " yes , yes , if you please . but be cautious how you tell he , if you think the news likely to agitate he . I be in no hurry . I can wait . you can call I when you think I can safely come up - stair . " 

 the surgeon nod , and softly ascend the narrow wooden stair lead to the upper chamber . 

 Robert Audley seat himself in a Windsor chair by the cold hearth - stone , and star disconsolately about he . but he be relieve at last by the low voice of the surgeon , who look down from the top of the little staircase to tell he that Luke Marks be awake , and would be glad to see he . 

 Robert immediately obey this summon . he creep softly up the stair , and take off his hat before he bend his head to enter at the low doorway of the humble rustic chamber . he take off his hat in the presence of this common peasant man , because he know that there be another and a more awful presence hover about the room , and eager to be admit . 

 Phoebe Marks be sit at the foot of the bed , with her eye fix upon her husband 's face not with any very tender expression in the pale light , but with a sharp , terrified anxiety , which show that it be the come of death itself that she dread , rather than the loss of her husband . the old woman be busy at the fire - place , air linen , and prepare some mess of broth which it be not likely the patient would ever eat . the sick man lie with his head prop up by pillow , his coarse face deadly pale , and his great hand wander uneasily about the coverlet . Phoebe have be read to he , for an open testament lie among the medicine and lotion bottle upon the table near the bed . every object in the room be neat and orderly , and bear witness of that delicate precision which have always be a distinguish characteristic of Phoebe . 

 the young woman rise as Robert Audley cross the threshold , and hurry toward he . 

 " let I speak to you for a moment , sir , before you talk to Luke , " she say , in an eager whisper . " pray let I speak to you first . " 

 " what be the gal a - sayin ' , there ? " ask the invalid in a subdue roar , which die away hoarsely on his lip . he be feebly savage , even in his weakness . the dull glaze of death be gather over his eye , but they still watch Phoebe with a sharp glance of dissatisfaction . " what be she up to there ? " he say . " I will not   have no plottin ' and no hatchin ' agen I . I want to speak to Mr. Audley my own self ; and whatever I do I be go to answer for . if I do any mischief , I be a - go to try and undo it . what be she a - sayin ' ? " 

 " she be not   a - sayin ' nothing , lovey , " answer the old woman , go to the bedside of her son , who even when make more interesting than usual by illness , do not seem a very fit subject for this tender appellation . 

 " she be only a - tellin ' the gentleman how bad you have   be , my pretty . " 

 " what I be a - go to tell I be only a - go to tell to he , remember , " growl Mr. Mark ; " and ketch I a - tellin ' of it to he if it warn't   for what he do for I the other night . " 

 " to be sure not , lovey , " answer the old woman soothingly . 

 Phoebe Marks have draw Mr. Audley out of the room and onto the narrow landing at the top of the little staircase . this landing be a platform of about three foot square , and it be as much as the two could manage to stand upon it without push each other against the whitewashed wall , or backward down the stair . 

 " oh , sir , I want to speak to you so badly , " Phoebe answer , eagerly ; " you know what I tell you when I find you safe and well upon the night of the fire ? " 

 " yes , yes . " 

 " I tell you what I suspect ; what I think still . " 

 " yes , I remember . " 

 " but I never breathe a word of it to anybody but you , sir , and I think that Luke have forget all about that night ; I think that what go before the fire have go clean out of his head altogether . he be tipsy , you know , when my la when she come to the Castle ; and I think he be so dazed and scar like by the fire that it all go out of his memory . he do not   suspect what I suspect , at any rate , or he would have speak of it to anybody or everybody ; but he be dreadful spiteful against my lady , for he say if she would have let he have a place at Brentwood or Chelmsford , this would not   have happen . so what I want to beg of you , sir , be not to let a word drop before Luke . " 

 " yes , yes , I understand ; I will be careful . " 

 " my lady have leave the Court , I hear , sir ? " 

 " yes . " 

 " never to come back , sir ? " 

 " never to come back . " 

 " but she have not go where she will be cruelly treat ; where she will be ill - used ? " 

 " no : she will be very kindly treat . " 

 " I be glad of that , sir ; I beg your pardon for trouble you with the question , sir , but my lady be a kind mistress to I . " 

 Luke 's voice , husky and feeble , be hear within the little chamber at this period of the conversation , demand angrily when " that gal would have do jawing ; " upon which Phoebe put her finger to her lip , and lead Mr. Audley back into the sick - room . 

 " I do not   want you " say Mr. Marks , decisively , as his wife re - enter the chamber " I do not   want you ; you have   no call to hear what I have   get to say I only want Mr. Audley , and I want to speak to he all alone , with none o ' your sneakin ' listenin ' at door , d'ye hear ? so you may go down - stair and keep there till you be want ; and you may take mother no , mother may stay , I shall want she presently . " 

 the sick man 's feeble hand point to the door , through which his wife depart very submissively . 

 " I have   no wish to hear anything , Luke , " she say , " but I hope you will not   say anything against those that have be good and generous to you . " 

 " I shall say what I like , " answer Mr. Marks , fiercely , " and I be not a - go to be order by you . you be not   the parson , as I have   ever heerd of ; nor the lawyer neither . " 

 the landlord of the Castle Inn have undergo no moral transformation by his death - bed suffering , fierce and rapid as they have be . perhaps some faint glimmer of a light that have be far off from his life now struggle feebly through the black obscurity of ignorance that darken his soul . perhaps a half angry , half sullen penitence urge he to make some rugged effort to atone for a life that have be selfish and drunken and wicked . be it how it might he wipe his white lip , and turn his haggard eye earnestly upon Robert Audley , point to a chair by the bedside . 

 " you make game of I in a general way , Mr. Audley , " he say , presently , " and you have   draw I out , and you have   tumble and toss I about like in a gentlemanly way , till I be nothink or anythink in your hand ; and you have   look I through and through , and turn I inside out till you think you know as much as I know . I have no particular call to be grateful to you , not before the fire at the Castle t'other night . but I be grateful to you for that . I be not grateful to folk in a general way , p'r'aps , because the thing as gentlefolk have give have a'most allus be the very thing I do not   want . they have   give I soup , and track , and flannel , and coal ; but , Lord , they have   make such a precious noise about it that I would have be to send them all back to them . but when a gentleman go and put his own life in danger to save a drunken brute like I , the drunken brute as ever be feel grateful like to that gentleman , and wish to say before he die which he see in the doctor 's face as he be not   get long to live ' thank ye , sir , I be oblige to you . " 

 Luke Marks stretch out his left hand the right hand have be injure by the fire , and be wrap in linen and grope feebly for that of Mr. Robert Audley . 

 the young man take the coarse but shrunken hand in both his own , and press it cordially . 

 " I need no thank , Luke Marks , " he say ; " I be very glad to be of service to you . " 

 Mr. Marks do not speak immediately . he be lie quietly upon his side , star reflectingly at Robert Audley . 

 " you be oncommon fond of that gent as disappear at the Court , warn't   you , sir ? " he say at last . 

 Robert start at the mention of his dead friend . 

 " you be oncommon fond of that Mr. Talboys , I have   hear say , sir , " repeat Luke . 

 " yes , yes , " answer Robert , rather impatiently , " he be my very dear friend . " 

 " I have   hear the servant at the Court say how you take on when you could not   find he . I have   heere the landlord of the Sun Inn say how cut up you be when you first miss he . ' if the two gent have be brother , ' the landlord say , ' our gent , ' meanin ' you , sir , ' could not   have be more cut up when he miss the other . ' "

 be he to be haunt forever by the ghost of his unburied friend ? he come here to comfort the sick man , and even here he be pursue by this relentless shadow ; even here he be remind of the secret crime which have darken his life .

" 

 Luke Marks look musingly at the earnest face of his visitor , and some shadowy expression , which be almost like a smile , flit feebly across the sick man 's haggard feature .

 " nothing . " 

 " then it be not   no good for I to try , " say the invalid , thoughtfully . " do she tell you ? " he ask , after a pause .

" I have already tell you that I do not wish to hear it speak of . whatever discovery you make , you make your market out of they . whatever guilty secret you get possession of , you be pay for keep silence . you have well keep silence to the end .  " I think so , most decidedly . you trade on your secret , and you be pay to keep it . it would be more honest to hold to your bargain , and keep it still . " 

 " but , suppose I want to tell something , " cry Luke , with feverish energy , ' suppose I feel I can not   die with a secret on my mind , and have ask to see you on purpose that I might tell you ; suppose that , and you will suppose nothing but the truth . I would have be burn alive before I would have tell she . " he speak these word between his set tooth , and scowl savagely as he utter they . " I would have be burn alive first . I make her pay for her pretty insolent way ; I make her pay for her air and grace ; I would never have tell she never , never !  the old woman pour out some cool drink into a mug , and carry it to her son . 

 he drink it in an eager hurry , as if he feel that the brief remainder of his life must be a race with the pitiless pedestrian , Time .

 Mr. Audley wonder where all this be to lead to , and how long he would have to sit by the sick man 's bed , hear a conversation that have no meaning to he .

 once more Mr. Audley start violently , and this time he look up earnestly at the face of the speaker , and listen , with a strange , breathless interest , that he scarcely understand himself , to what Luke Marks be say .

 the old woman nod , and mutter something to the effect that she remember all these circumstance most vividly , now that Luke happen to mention they . 

 Robert Audley utter a wild cry , and fall down upon his knee by the side of the sick man 's bed .

 the first paper which Robert Audley have unfold contain the follow line , write in that cramp , yet scrawl hand which be so strange to he : 

 " MY DEAR FRIEND I write to you in such utter confusion of mind as perhaps no man ever before suffer . I can not tell you what have happen to I , I can only tell you that something have happen which will drive I from England a break - hearted man , to seek some corner of the earth in which I may live and die unknown and forgotten . I can only ask you to forget I . if your friendship could have do I any good , I would have appeal to it . if your counsel could have be any help to I , I would have confide in you . but neither friendship nor counsel can help I ; and all I can say to you be this , God bless you for the past , and teach you to forget I in the future . G.T. " 

 the second paper be address to another person , and its content be brief than those of the first .

 Robert Audley sit star at these line in hopeless bewilderment . they be not in his friend 's familiar hand , and yet they purport to be write by he and be sign with his initial .

 " I be at work up at Atkinson 's farm , last September , " say Luke Marks , " help to stack the last of the corn , and as the nighest way from the farm to mother 's cottage be through the meadow at the back of the Court , I use to come that way , and Phoebe use to stand in the garden wall beyond the lime - walk sometimes , to have a chat with I , knowin ' my time o ' comin ' home .

Audley church clock strike nine as I be crossin ' the meadow between Atkinson 's and the Court , and it must have be about a quarter past nine when I get into the kitchen garden . 

 " I cross the garden , and go into the lime - walk ; the nigh way to the servant ' hall take I through the shrubbery and past the dry well . it be a dark night , but I know my way well enough about the old place , and the light in the window of the servant ' hall look red and comfortable through the darkness . I be close against the mouth of the dry well when I hear a sound that make my blood creep . it be a groan a groan of a man in pain , as be lyin ' somewhere hide among the bush . I warn't   afraid of ghost and I warn't   afraid of anythink in a general way , but there be somethin in hearin ' this groan as chill I to the very heart , and for a minute I be strike all of a heap , and do not   know what to do . but I hear the groan again , and then I begin to search among the bush . ' there be broken heart as well as break limb , and they be not so easy mend . '

 " I know that the key be mostly leave in the wooden gate in the garden wall , so I lead he that way . he could scarcely walk at first , and it be only by leanin ' heavily upon my shoulder that he manage to get along .  Luke Marks have finish his story , and lie quietly enough , exhaust by have talk so long . he watch Robert Audley 's face , fully expect some reproof , some grave lecture ; for he have a vague consciousness that he have do wrong .

 CHAPTER XL . 

 RESTORED . 

 Clara Talboys return to dorsetshire , to tell her father that his only son have sail for Australia upon the 9th of September , and that it be most probable he yet live , and would return to claim the forgiveness of the father he have never very particularly injure ; except in the matter of have make that terrible matrimonial mistake which have exercise so fatal an influence upon his youth . 

 Mr. Harcourt - Talboys be fairly nonplus . Junius Brutus have never be place in such a position as this , and see no way of get out of this dilemma by act after his favorite model , Mr. Talboys be fain to be natural for once in his life , and to confess that he have suffer much uneasiness and pain of mind about his only son since his conversation with Robert Audley , and that he would be heartily glad to take his poor boy to his arm , whenever he should return to England . but when be he likely to return ? and how be he to be communicate with ? that be the question . Robert Audley remember the advertisement which he have cause to be insert in the Melbourne and Sydney paper . if George have re - enter either city alive , how be it that no notice have ever be take of that advertisement ? be it likely that his friend would be indifferent to his uneasiness ? but then , again , it be just possible that George Talboys have not happen to see this advertisement ; and , as he have travel under a feigned name , neither his fellow passenger nor the captain of the vessel would have be able to identify he with the person advertise for . what be to be do ? must they wait patiently till George grow weary of his exile , and return to his friend who love he ? or be there any mean to be take by which his return might be hasten ? Robert Audley be at fault ! perhaps , in the unspeakable relief of mind which he have experience upon the discovery of his friend 's escape , he be unable to look beyond the one fact of that providential preservation . 

 in this state of mind he go down to dorsetshire to pay a visit to Mr. Talboys , who have give way to a perfect torrent of generous impulse , and have go so far as to invite his son 's friend to share the prim hospitality of the square , red brick mansion . 

 Mr. Talboys have only two sentiment upon the subject of George 's story ; one be a natural relief and happiness in the thought that his son have be save , the other be an earnest wish that my lady have be his wife , and that he might thus have have the pleasure of make a signal example of she . 

 " it be not for I to blame you , Mr. Audley , " he say , " for have smuggle this guilty woman out of the reach of justice , and thus , as I may say , palter with the law of your country . I can only remark that , have the lady fall into my hand , she would have be very differently treat . " 

 it be in the middle of April when Robert Audley find himself once more under those black fir - tree beneath which his wander thought have so often stay since his first meeting with Clara Talboys . there be primrose and early violet in the hedge now , and the stream , which , upon his first visit , have be hard and frost - bind as the heart of Harcourt Talboys , have thaw , like that gentleman , and run merrily under the blackthorn bush in the capricious April sunshine . 

 Robert have a prim bedroom , and an uncompromise dressing - room allot he in the square house , and he wake every morning upon a metallic spring mattress , which always give he the idea of sleep upon some musical instrument , to see the sun glare in upon he through the square , white blind and light up the two lackered urn which adorn the foot of the blue iron bedstead , until they blaze like two tiny brazen lamp of the roman period . he emulate Mr. Harcourt Talboys in the matter of shower - bath and cold water , and emerge prim and blue as that gentleman himself , as the clock in the hall strike seven , to join the master of the house in his ante - breakfast constitutional under the fir - tree in the stiff plantation . 

 but there be generally a third person who assist in the constitutional promenade , and that third person be Clara Talboys , who use to walk by her father 's side , more beautiful than the morning for that be sometimes dull and cloudy , while she be always fresh and bright in a broad - leave straw - hat and flap blue ribbon , one quarter of an inch of which Mr. Audley would have esteem a prouder decoration than ever adorn a favor creature 's button - hole . 

 at first they be very ceremonious toward each other , and be only familiar and friendly upon the one subject of George 's adventure ; but little by little a pleasant intimacy arise between they , and before the first three week of Robert 's visit have elapse , Miss Talboys make he happy , by take he seriously in hand and lecture he on the purposeless life he have lead so long , and the little use he have make of the talent and opportunity that have be give to he . 

 how pleasant it be to be lecture by the woman he love ! how pleasant it be to humiliate himself and depreciate himself before she ! how delightful it be to get such splendid opportunity of hint that if his life have be sanctify by an object he might indeed have strive to be something well than an idle flaneur upon the smooth pathway that have no particular goal ; that , bless by the tie which would have give a solemn purpose to every hour of his existence , he might indeed have fight the battle earnestly and unflinchingly . he generally wound up with a gloomy insinuation to the effect that it be only likely he would drop quietly over the edge of the Temple Gardens some afternoon when the river be bright and placid in the low sunlight , and the little child have go home to their tea . 

 " do you think I can read french novel and smoke mild turkish until I be three - score - and - ten , Miss Talboys ? " he ask . " do you think there will not come a day in which my meerschaum will be foul , and the french novel more than usually stupid , and life altogether such a dismal monotony that I shall want to get rid of it somehow or other ? " 

 I be sorry to say that while this hypocritical young barrister be hold forth in this despondent way , he have mentally sell up his bachelor possession , include all Michel Levy 's publication , and half a dozen solid silver - mount meerschaum ; pension off Mrs. Maloney , and lay out two or three thousand pound in the purchase of a few acre of verdant shrubbery and sloping lawn , embosome amid which there should be a fairy cottage ornťe , whose rustic casement should glimmer out of bower of myrtle and clematis to see themselves reflect in the purple bosom of the lake . 

 of course , Clara Talboys be far from discover the drift of these melancholy lamentation . she recommend Mr. Audley to read hard and think seriously of his profession , and begin life in real earnest . it be a hard , dry sort of existence , perhaps , which she recommend ; a life of serious work and application , in which he should strive to be useful to his fellow - creature , and win a reputation for himself . 

 " I would do all that , " he think , " and do it earnestly , if I could be sure of a reward for my labor . if she would accept my reputation when it be win , and support I in the struggle by her beloved companionship . but what if she send I away to fight the battle , and marry some hulking country squire while my back be turn ? " 

 be naturally of a vacillating and dilatory disposition , there be no saying how long Mr. Audley might have keep his secret , fearful to speak and break the charm of that uncertainty which , though not always hopeful , be very seldom quite despairing , have not he be hurry by the impulse of an unguarded moment into a full confession of the truth . 

 he have stay five week at Grange Heath , and feel that he could not , in common decency , stay any long ; so he have pack his portmanteau one pleasant May morning , and have announce his departure . 

 Mr. Talboys be not the sort of man to utter any passionate lamentation at the prospect of lose his guest , but he express himself with a cool cordiality which serve with he as the strong demonstration of friendship . 

 " we have get on very well together , Mr. Audley , " he say , " and you have be pleased to appear sufficiently happy in the quiet routine of our orderly household ; nay , more , you have conform to our little domestic regulation in a manner which I can not refrain from say I take as an especial compliment to myself . " 

 Robert bow . how thankful he be to the good fortune which have never suffer he to oversleep the signal of the clang bell , or lead he away beyond the ken of clock at Mr. Talboys ' luncheon hour . 

 " I trust as we have get on so remarkably well together , " Mr. Talboys resume , " you will do I the honor of repeat your visit to dorsetshire whenever you feel inclined . you will find plenty of sport among my farm , and you will meet with every politeness and attention from my tenant , if you like to bring your gun with you . " 

 Robert respond most heartily to these friendly overture . he declare that there be no earthly occupation that be more agreeable to he than partridge - shooting , and that he should be only too delighted to avail himself of the privilege so kindly offer to he . he could not help glance toward Clara as he say this . the perfect lid droop a little over the brown eye , and the faint shadow of a blush illuminate the beautiful face .

 but in the evening after dinner , when the sun be low in the west , and Harcourt Talboys closet in his library upon some judicial business with his lawyer and a tenant farmer , Mr. Audley grow a little more agreeable . he stand by Clara 's side in one of the long window of the drawing - room , watch the shadow deepen in the sky and the rosy light grow every moment rosier as the sun die out . he could not help enjoy that quiet tete - a - tete , though the shadow of the next morning 's express which be to carry he away to London loom darkly across the pathway of his joy . he could not help be happy in her presence ; forgetful of the past , reckless of the future .

 " and do you think , Clara , that I should think any sacrifice too great a one if it be make for you ? do you think there be any voyage I would refuse to take , if I know that you would welcome I when I come home , and thank I for have serve you faithfully ? I will go from one end of the continent of Australia to the other to look for your brother , if you please , Clara ; and will never return alive unless I bring he with I , and will take my chance of what reward you shall give I for my labor .  " shall we both go , dearest ? shall we go as man and wife ? shall we go together , my dear love , and bring our brother back between we ? " 

 Mr. Harcourt Talboys , come into the lamplit room a quarter of an hour afterward , find Robert Audley alone , and have to listen to a revelation which very much surprise he . like all self - sufficient people , he be tolerably blind to everything that happen under his nose , and he have fully believe that his own society , and the spartan regularity of his household , have be the attraction which have make dorsetshire delightful to his guest .

 George Talboys speak very briefly of that sunny seventh of September , upon which he have leave his friend sleep by the trout stream while he go to accuse his false wife of that conspiracy which have well nigh break his heart . 

 " God know that from the moment in which I sink into the black pit , know the treacherous hand that have send I to what might have be my death , my chief thought be of the safety of the woman who have betray I . I be stun and daze for a few minute , but I rouse myself by an effort , for I feel that the atmosphere I breathe be deadly . I have my australian experience to help I in my peril ; I could climb like a cat . the stone of which the well be build be rugged and irregular , and I be able to work my way upward by plant my foot in the interstice of the stone , and rest my back at time against the opposite side of the well , help myself as well as I could with my hand , though one arm be crippled . it be hard work , Bob , and it seem strange that a man who have long profess himself weary of his life , should take so much trouble to preserve it . I think I must have be work upward of half an hour before I get to the top ; I know the time seem an eternity of pain and peril . it be impossible for I to leave the place until after dark without be observe , so I hide myself behind a clump of laurel - bush , and lie down on the grass faint and exhausted to wait for nightfall . the man who find I there tell you the rest . Robert . " 

 " yes , my poor old friend . yes , he tell I all . " 

 George have never return to Australia after all . he have go on board the Victoria Regia , but have afterward change his berth for one in another vessel belong to the same owner , and have go to New York , where he have stay as long as he could endure the loneliness of an existence which separate he from every friend he have ever know . 

 " Jonathan be very kind to I , Bob , " he say ; " I have enough money to enable I to get on pretty well in my own quiet way and I mean to have start for the California gold field to get more when that be go . I might have make plenty of friend have I please , but I carry the old bullet in my breast ; and what sympathy could I have with man who know nothing of my grief ? I yearn for the strong grasp of your hand , Bob ; the friendly touch of the hand which have guide I through the dark passage of my life . " 

 CHAPTER XLI . 

 AT PEACE . 

 two year have pass since the May twilight in which Robert find his old friend ; and Mr. Audley 's dream of a fairy cottage have be realize between Teddington Locks and Hampton Bridge , where , amid a little forest of foliage , there be a fantastical dwelling place of rustic woodwork , whose latticed window look out upon the river . here , among the lily and the rush on the slop bank , a brave boy of eight year old play with a toddle baby , who peer wonderingly from his nurse 's arm at that other baby in the purple depth of the quiet water . 

 Mr. Audley be a rise man upon the home circuit by this time , and have distinguish himself in the great breach of promise case of Hobbs v. Nobbs , and have convulse the court by his deliciously comic rendering of the faithless Nobb 's amatory correspondence . the handsome dark - eyed boy be Master George Talboys , who decline musa at Eton , and fish for tadpole in the clear water under the spread umbrage beyond the ivied wall of the academy . but he come very often to the fairy cottage to see his father , who live there with his sister and his sister 's husband ; and he be very happy with his Uncle Robert , his Aunt Clara , and the pretty baby who have just begin to toddle on the smooth lawn that slop down to the water 's brink , upon which there be a little swiss boat - house and landing - stage where Robert and George moor their slender wherry . 

 other people come to the cottage near Teddington . a bright , merry - hearted girl , and a gray - bearded gentleman , who have survive the trouble of his life , and battle with it as a Christian should . 

 it be more than a year since a black - edged letter , write upon foreign paper , come to Robert Audley , to announce the death of a certain Madame Taylor , who have expire peacefully at villebrumeuse , die after a long illness , which Monsieur Val describe as a maladie de langueur . 

 another visitor come to the cottage in this bright summer of 1861 a frank , generous hearted young man , who toss the baby and play with Georgey , and be especially great in the management of the boat , which be never idle when Sir Harry Towers be at Teddington . 

 there be a pretty rustic smoking - room over the Swiss boat - house , in which the gentleman sit and smoke in the summer evening , and whence they be summon by Clara and Alicia to drink tea , and eat strawberry and cream upon the lawn . 

 Audley Court be shut up , and a grim old housekeeper reign paramount in the mansion which my lady 's ring laughter once make musical . a curtain hang before the pre - raphaelite portrait ; and the blue mold which artist dread gather upon the Wouvermans and Poussins , the Cuyps and Tintorettis . the house be often show to inquisitive visitor , though the baronet be not inform of that fact , and people admire my lady 's room , and ask many question about the pretty , fair - haired woman who die abroad . 

 Sir Michael have no fancy to return to the familiar dwelling - place in which he once dream a brief dream of impossible happiness . he remain in London until Alicia shall be Lady Towers , when he be to remove to a house he have lately buy in Hertfordshire , on the border of his son - in - law 's estate . George Talboys be very happy with his sister and his old friend . he be a young man yet , remember , and it be not quite impossible that he may , by - and - by , find some one who will console he for the past . that dark story of the past fade little by little every day , and there may come a time in which the shadow my lady 's wickedness have cast upon the young man 's life will utterly vanish away . 

 the meerschaum and the french novel have be present to a young Templar with whom Robert Audley have be friendly in his bachelor day ; and Mrs. Maloney have a little pension , pay she quarterly , for her care of the canary and geranium . 

 I hope no one will take objection to my story because the end of it leave the good people all happy and at peace . if my experience of life have not be very long , it have at least be manifold ; and I can safely subscribe to that which a mighty king and a great philosopher declare , when he say , that neither the experience of his youth nor of his age have ever show he " the righteous forsaken , nor his seed beg their bread . " 

 the END .
